Franco-German Envy Will Make the Four-Power Pact a Bubble 65

French Premier Announces Foreign Policy in the Chamber of Deputies

Foreign Minister Peng Gu's Draft Note Sent Out Today

(Havas, Paris, 7th) Regarding the four-power pact proposed by Britain and Italy, a memorandum has been drafted by Foreign Minister Peng Gu and the head of the foreign affairs department. The text is very short, first explaining the principles, followed by specific recommendations, all based on Article 10 of the League of Nations Covenant regarding administrative integrity and political independence, Article 16 regarding sanctions against aggression, and Article 19 regarding the procedure for revising treaties. This memorandum, in addition to political clauses, clarifies the benefits of economic cooperation among the four powers. In other words, it reiterates the French theory of European integration. The full text will be sent to London and Rome tomorrow.

(Reuters, Berlin, 6th) Today, a semi-official report stated that the four-power agreement proposed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has lost its original appearance after being revised by France, and therefore can no longer be accepted by Germany.

(Reuters, Paris, 6th) French Premier Daladier delivered a long-awaited foreign policy speech in the Chamber of Deputies today, expressing France's concern about the situation in Germany and asking a question: "In view of a revitalized nationalism, should Europe redraw the map to seek peace?" Daladier continued that France intends to pursue a construction policy and opposes the supervisory power of major countries, which is even more ambitious than the Holy Alliance. Any agreement must logically be based on the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the Locarno Pact, and the entire League of Nations Covenant, and not based on a part of the Covenant, so that this revision will not lead to envy among the countries. France will propose practical amendments to the British disarmament plan, but France very much hopes that Britain's faithful efforts will be completely successful. In his speech, Daladier praised Britain and Italy, and then mentioned the economic sphere, saying that he was willing to gladly acknowledge the goodwill expressed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini towards France. After the speech, the Chamber of Deputies passed a vote of confidence in the government by a vote of 430 to 107.

(Reuters, Paris, 6th) French Foreign Minister Peng Gu said in a speech before the vote of confidence in the Chamber of Deputies today that Germany's merger of political and police organs into one is a violation of the peace treaty. France is now consulting with the signatory countries of the Locarno Pact and Germany, and if necessary, will propose this matter in Geneva. He then said that the Disarmament Conference is now encountering opposition from the Italian-German group, and if this group continues, it will cause tomorrow's war in Europe. Peng Gu also praised Britain's loyalty and finally said that Italy's proposal should be considered so that the four powers can cooperate on related issues.

(Havas, Warsaw, 7th) A reporter from the "Polish Post" interviewed Czech Foreign Minister Benes and asked him to express his opinion on the Four-Power Pact. Benes declared, "If the establishment of the Four-Power Club is followed by a majority club, as some people expect, then the world will fall into complete chaos. If the four powers can conclude a treaty, why can't Poland and the Little Entente conclude a treaty with each other? If the major powers want to interfere in our affairs, why can't we interfere in the affairs of the major powers? And Russia can also unite with China to create a two-country club and focus their eyes on British India. The intention of the Four-Power Pact is to hope for peace, but the result is the opposite. Once the Four-Power Pact is concluded, if any events related to us are discussed by the four powers, we should answer, 'Why not go to Geneva?' We dare to believe that if the Little Entente countries and Poland declare that they will withdraw from the League of Nations after the Four-Power Pact is concluded, then the Four-Power Pact will not be established. In short, if the Four-Power Pact is concluded, the League of Nations will be destroyed as a rubble field."

(Havas, London, 7th) Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu is very active here. This morning, he visited the Polish Ambassador and the Greek Minister. At noon, he will have lunch with former Finance Minister Chamberlain. After lunch, he will go to the Foreign Office and meet with Sir Lawrence at the Treasury. In the evening, he will have dinner with the ministers of the Little Entente countries stationed in London and will leave London tomorrow morning.

United States Reorganizes Navy 66

Allocates $46 Million to Build Ships

Strives to Reduce Naval Administrative Expenses

(National News Agency, Washington, 6th) Although the United States still supports the reduction of armaments, and its leaders will soon meet with British and French authorities to discuss this matter, the situation in Congress today clearly indicates a firm trend towards building new ships. Vincent, Chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee, met with Navy Secretary Swanson today to discuss the ship construction program. It is reported that Swanson generally agreed with the plan to allocate $46 million for the next year, saying that he would be very pleased if Congress could pass this ship construction budget. In addition to Swanson and Vincent discussing the ship construction program, Senator Trammell also introduced a bill today stipulating the construction of new ships to reach treaty limits. It has now been transferred to the Senate Naval Affairs Committee for review. However, naval administrative expenses are being reduced as much as possible. The measures to save funds ordered by the former and current presidents were implemented today by order of the Navy Department. In the future, each naval shipyard will work five and a half days a week, affecting a total of 44,000 people. All officers in charge of construction and repair and all soldiers and non-military employees must comply. However, this order is not enough to reduce naval effectiveness, and in practice can maintain the existing staff, otherwise there will inevitably be reductions.

(National News Agency, Washington, 6th) Senator Trammell today introduced a new ship construction bill, specifically stipulating that at least $46 million should be allocated in 1929 to begin construction of five of the fifteen cruisers authorized to be built in 1929, all of which are 10,000-ton cruisers equipped with 6-inch guns, and that two aircraft carriers should be built to replace the old ships, and one 10,000-ton cruiser equipped with an aviation deck to replace the...

...the old ship Rochester, which is about to be dismantled. According to the cruisers passed in 1929, all of them are equipped with 8-inch guns, but after being canceled by the London Treaty, they will now be equipped with 6-inch guns. This ship construction plan will actually complete the warships permitted by the London Treaty. Trammell's case is nothing more than a response to the warning issued by Vincent, Chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee, yesterday morning that if new ships are not built immediately, the US naval force will be reduced to fifth place within three years. Vincent is the chairman of the House Naval Affairs Committee and a close friend of the US President, and what he says can usually be regarded as having the President's consent. It is also noted that the House has previously passed a bill stipulating the construction of nine cruisers, three submarines, and three destroyers to replace the old ships. Several of these cruisers were passed in 1929, but if Trammell's new proposal can be passed in the Senate, it will be transferred to the House to replace the previous bill.

Beer Prohibition Lifted, All Kinds of Scenes 67

A Spectacle Not Seen in the United States for Many Years

(National News Agency, New York, 7th) At 0:01 this morning (i.e., 12:01 AM), a black hearse, followed by six black-robed pallbearers with solemn demeanor, proceeded from Metley to Broadway. Inside the hearse was a barrel of "near beer," the only drink that those with a craving for yeast had been able to obtain after the prohibition. On this day of lifting the prohibition, it was especially sent to its final resting place. When the hearse arrived in the city center, the pallbearers dumped the "near beer" into the ditch. Then, the accompanying band played a marching song to welcome the return of beer to the United States. At this time, all the hotels, nightclubs, restaurants, and clubs were full. Although the New York Brewers Association decided to start delivering goods only at 7:00 this morning, these drinkers all had a glass in hand, celebrating the lifting of the ban. A huge supply of beer manufactured in the Midwest of the United States was transported to New York by plane and express train. Although there was wild rejoicing everywhere, the order was still good. Today, only nineteen states have issued state laws and police regulations allowing the sale of beer. However, breweries in these nineteen states began delivering beer as soon as the bell rang "thirteen" yesterday, such as in Milwaukee, St. Louis, Chicago, and St. Paul. At first, they used horse-drawn carts to deliver beer, and then they used motor vehicles. When these teams of black horses passed through the thoroughfare, it was not only a spectacle not seen in the United States for many years, but it also made people wonder how so many horses could be found.

Feng Writes Letter to Chiang, Offering Suggestions for Resisting Japan 69

Results of Huang Shao-hong's Visit to Feng

Expeditiously Transfer All National Troops to Concentrate on Resisting Japan

Hopes Chiang Will Personally Lead the Army to Unify Authority

Especially Hopes for Practical Implementation and Execution

(Ping News) Minister of the Interior Huang Shao-hong, under the order of Military Affairs Commission Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, went to Zhangjiakou to visit Feng Yuxiang, inviting Feng to go to Beijing to discuss the major plan of resisting Japan. After Huang returned to Ping, he took the Pingpu train to Beijing at 5:15 p.m. on the 4th to report everything to Chiang. It is reported that Feng personally wrote a letter to Chiang on the major plan of resisting Japan, putting forward concrete measures to urge Chiang to implement them. The letter was handed over by Huang to be presented. The original letter is as follows:

"Elder Brother Jieshi,

I received your reply through Comrade Xiwen, who returned from Baoding, and I have read your letter from Jikuan Zhemin, who came to a stop. Your diligence for the country is admirable. I, Xiang, foolishly believe that desperately resisting the Japanese bandits and using all our strength to recover the lost territories as soon as possible is the only important thing today. Even for your personal sake, for the sake of the country, and for the sake of the nation, there is no second path to take. However, the method of resistance should not be to resist only when they attack. If they do not attack, we will just sit and wait for them to attack. Currently, my humble opinion on the method of resistance is as follows:

(1) Quickly find a way to transfer 80% of the troops to the front, dividing them into concentrated areas.

(2) Allocate 80% of the military expenditure for the purpose of resisting Japan.

(3) You, Elder Brother, should personally take command to unify authority. If you cannot go, please have Mr. Li Ren-chao take command. This person has bloodiness and conscience and is a true and sincere patriotic hero. Moreover, he has been your Chief of Staff for many years.

(4) Comrades Cai Tingkai, Jiang Guangnai, and Dai Ji are brave and good at fighting and full of sacrifice. Cai can lead 50,000 people, Jiang can lead 50,000 people, and Dai can lead 30,000 people, all under the command of Comrade Chen Mingshu, or under your command, as they have experience in resisting Japan.

(5) Song Zheyuan can fight desperately, and Sun Dianying is not afraid of death. Each can lead 50,000 people. If their subordinates are insufficient, allocate them.

(6) Comrade Zhang Fakui is wholeheartedly for the country and has worked hard for the revolution. You, Elder Brother, have known him deeply for a long time. For the sake of national survival, please truly put the past aside and allocate 40,000 troops to his command. He will definitely have a great effect on recovering the lost territories.

(7) Hu Yukun is a hero of the Northeast and a gentleman of integrity. If 50,000 troops can be allocated to his command, he will definitely serve his hometown.

(8) Mr. Jiang Baili and Mr. Huang Yingbai not only have profound military knowledge but also have far-sighted views on national planning. If you ask them to participate in the calculations for resisting Japan, they will definitely offer great strategies.

(9) Mr. Ma Xiangbo, Zhu Ziqiao, Sa Zhenbing, Wang Tieshan, Huang Renzhi, and Zhang Zhongren are all full of love for the country and the people and are great figures of integrity, honesty, and trustworthiness. If you find a way to invite them together and ask them to point out the ways to save the country and the people, they will definitely have righteous methods to relieve the suffering of the people. (10) Grant amnesty to political prisoners and immediately implement freedom of speech, assembly, and association to allow grievances to be expressed and unequal grievances to be voiced. (11) Comrades Hu Hanmin, Wang Jingwei, Yu Youren, Ju Juesheng, Sun Zhesheng, and Li Xiehe each have a kind of hard bone and a kind of chivalrous spirit. Not only is their knowledge high and far-reaching, but their love for the country and the people is even richer. Please take two hours each day to have long and detailed discussions with them. They will definitely be of great help to national affairs. However, do not waste time and speak official language. (12) The country's affairs have become so bad. Of course, many friends cannot escape their blame, but you and I cannot but bear some responsibility. Today's disapproval of evil and even more recognition of sins and admitting mistakes to compatriots across the country are not the actions of a bright gentleman. Especially hope that you, Elder Brother, will advocate it. The above twelve articles are the heartfelt words I, Xiang, have offered to you. Because of your sincere inquiries, Elder Brother, I, Xiang, have learned something and dare not fail to contribute my humble opinions. Practice, work, act, and implement are the basis of all success. There have been not a few declarations in the past, and there are not a few regulations, but there is nothing that does not lack implementation. Especially hope that you, Elder Brother, will pay attention to this three times. I, Xiang, am terrified of the country's demise and offer these words sincerely. I ask Comrades Huang and Xiong to express the rest in person. The South is in sight, and I cannot bear to be parted. Please take care of the country and yourself.

Your Younger Brother, Feng Yuxiang, Bowed and Signed. 22, 3, 30."

Chairman Chiang Arrives in Jiangxi 70

Arrives in Xun by Ship and Then Takes a Special Train to Nanchang

Orders the Transfer of Large Armies to Quickly Eliminate the Bandits

(Nanchang Correspondence) Chairman Chiang took the Chu You warship west from Beijing at noon on the 4th and arrived in Xun at 6:30 p.m. on the 5th. Xiong Shihui had received the news in advance, so he went from the province to Xun on the morning of the 5th to welcome him. When the Chu You warship was anchored in Xun, Xiong boarded the ship to meet with Chiang, reporting on the situation of the Red bandits' rampant activity after Chiang went north, the suppression of the Red Army, the recent incursion of Zhu and Mao into Xingan Qingjiang, the situation of the suppression, and the general situation of the province's post-disaster reconstruction. Chiang then accompanied Xiong ashore, took a car to the train station, and transferred to a special train on the Nanxun Railway to the province. At about 1:00 a.m. late at night, the special train arrived at Niuxing Station. Those who welcomed him at the station included He Guoguang, Chief of Staff of the Three-Province Bandit Suppression Headquarters, Lai Yingwei, Commander of the City Defense, Dai Yue, Brigade Commander of the Independent 36th Brigade, and dozens of senior officials from various agencies. After Chiang got off the train and exchanged greetings with the welcoming personnel, he took a ferry across the river under strict guard and then took a car directly to the Science Museum to stay. It is reported that Chiang's arrival, in addition to commanding the Central Route Chen Cheng, the Left Route Cai Tingkai, and the Right Route Yu Hanmou's troops to converge in Ruijin in the shortest possible time to eliminate Zhu, Mao, and Peng, also ordered the transfer of troops from Zhejiang, Anhui, Hunan, and Hubei to advance to the borders of Jiangxi at the same time to annihilate Fang, Shao, Kong Hechong, and Li Tianzhu's forces. With a force of more than 300,000, the Jiangxi bandits can be wiped out in one fell swoop. Two days ago, Zhu and Mao's pseudo-First Front Army penetrated deeply into Xingan from Le'an, attempting to spy on the provincial capital from Qingjiang, causing great panic among the people. Now that Chiang has arrived in Jiangxi to sit down, the hearts of the people are greatly reassured. After receiving the news of Chiang's arrival in Jiangxi, the morale of the troops on the front line has also been greatly boosted. Chen Cheng has ordered his troops to obliquely cross □□ and flank the bandits in Xingan. Sun Lianzhong's troops are advancing south from Zhangshu, and certain two troops from Yuanhe and Jihe are also advancing towards Xingan, taking a four-sided encirclement approach to eliminate the bandits of Zhu and Mao's pseudo-131st Army Corps between Xingan and Yongfeng. (April 6)

County Magistrate of Zhangqiu Stands in a Wooden Cage 71

Secretary and Bureau Chief Kneel as Punishment

New Drama of Han Fuju's Inspection Tour

Jinan Dispatch: Shandong Province Chairman Han Fuju, accompanied by Zhang Liansheng, Yao Yijie, Sha Yuebo, and others, departed from Jinan at noon on the 4th to inspect eastern Shandong and review county administration. They arrived at Zaoyuan Station at 3:30 PM and entered the city by car at 4:00 PM. At 6:00 PM, he convened a roll call of all government agencies, where the county government secretary and Public Security Bureau Chief Ma Dianbang were ordered to kneel as punishment. The Public Security Bureau Chief was also fined 50 yuan per month. That evening, they stayed at the Yan Gongdian Inn. At 5:00 AM the next morning, he convened a motivational meeting for all government personnel at the county government office. At 6:00 AM, he inspected the detention center. There was a case in which the county magistrate, Feng Yonghe, and the court had mishandled the trial, resulting in a wrongful imprisonment. Han was extremely enraged and ordered the county magistrate, the judge, and the prosecutor to be confined in wooden cages, intending to severely punish them. After local figures pleaded for leniency, they were released. The county magistrate immediately requested a disciplinary action and was given a demerit. The County Public Security Bureau originally had a first-class establishment with four branch offices. After Han inspected the bureau, he ordered it to be changed to a third-class county establishment, completely abolishing the four branch offices. He also instructed the county magistrate to work with the Third Section to handle the matter. Around 10:00 AM, Han heard cases in the county government hall, totaling twelve. After the hearings, he made a brief statement, saying that lawsuits are not for the poor because the law does not protect them. He then gathered the public for an open-air speech. At 11:00 AM, he left the county government office by car to Zaoyuan Station and departed eastward to Qingcheng for inspection (5th).

Three Companies Sign Submarine Cable Contract 72

Canceling Submarine Cable Landing Patent Rights

Recovering the Right to Directly Send and Receive Telegrams

Beijing Dispatch: The Ministry of Transportation has been urging the signing of the submarine cable contract with Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific companies, which had been approved by the National Government. Negotiations have been ongoing for years. The companies finally sent representatives to the Ministry of Transportation on the 5th to apply for submarine cable landing licenses and officially signed the contract with the Ministry's Directorate General of Telecommunications. The entire process and content of the contract are detailed below.

Process of Revising the Contract 73

The Great Eastern, Great Northern, and Pacific companies have been operating international telecommunications businesses in China for more than sixty years. All previous contracts contained many provisions that compromised Chinese sovereignty, especially the companies' establishment of receiving and transmitting offices in Shanghai, which granted them the right to directly send and receive telegrams. In December of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the Ministry of Transportation, aware that all these contracts would expire at the end of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), stipulated that one year's advance notice of termination be given. The Ministry promptly notified the companies that all previous contracts would be terminated on January 1, 1931, and informed the Ministries of Foreign Affairs to notify the British and Danish envoys in China. At the same time, the Ministry formally invited the companies to send representatives to the Ministry to discuss the closing matters and future communication arrangements. It was not until the end of March of the 19th year of the Republic (1930) that the companies sent representatives to negotiate. Initially, they demanded permanent submarine cable landing patent rights and insisted that the revised contract should be based on the old contracts. Subsequently, they refused to relinquish the right to receive and transmit telegrams and refused to increase the share of telegraph fees. In all respects, they wanted to maintain their original status. The Ministry of Transportation argued on principle. After nine months, as the contract expired at the end of December of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), the companies finally relented. The Ministry then drafted a tentative contract for resolution in accordance with the principles decided by the State Council. From January of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), separate meetings were held. After four months of discussions, an agreement was reached, and the Ministry submitted the draft to the Executive Yuan, which then submitted it to the National Government for review. The companies then sought instructions from their headquarters in order to sign the contract. In December of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the contract was approved by the National Government and ordered to be signed. However, the companies took advantage of the outbreak of the Eastern Provinces Incident (Mukden Incident) and the tense diplomatic situation to delay signing the contract. The Ministry of Transportation was unable to proceed, and another year was lost.

Circumstances of Urging the Contract Signing 74

Recently, Zhu Jia-hua succeeded as Minister of Transportation. Regarding this revised contract, he deeply felt that, while the gains may not be as satisfactory as desired, the case had been decided by the National Government. The companies, taking advantage of the delay, continued to maintain the status quo and acted independently without being subject to the Ministry's control during this period when there was no contractual constraint. If a resolution was not reached quickly, it would become a de facto recognition, causing even greater damage to national sovereignty. During the Shanghai Incident, the companies refused to allow inspections of telegram transmissions and arbitrarily laid temporary cables in the Huangpu River, as clear evidence of their actions. Consequently, the Directorate General of Telecommunications was instructed to urgently negotiate with the companies and urge them to sign the contract and apply for submarine cable landing licenses. Unexpectedly, the companies continued to create obstacles and delay the process. Following repeated urging from the Ministry, they proposed modifications: (1) The contract should be primarily in English; (2) Price reductions in telegram fees should not require our consent; (3) Route identification and direct routing of telegrams should be explicitly included in the contract; (4) The companies' right to receive and transmit telegrams should be maintained. The Ministry rejected the modifications, stating that the matter had already been decided. The companies then used the pretext of seeking instructions from their headquarters to further delay the process. Having no choice, the Ministry, on January 18, again refuted in detail the four points of modification requested by the companies and set a deadline of February 15 of this year for the contract to be signed in its original form, without any modifications, and for the licenses to be obtained. Otherwise, appropriate and effective measures would be taken, and the companies would bear the responsibility. The companies did not send representatives to the Directorate General of Telecommunications until February 14. On February 15, they met with Minister Zhu, reiterated the previous four demands, and insisted on equal treatment. They stated that they needed to seek further instructions from their respective governments before responding. To achieve a satisfactory outcome, the Ministry granted a discretionary extension. Subsequently, the British envoy negotiated with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which in turn sent a letter to the Ministry, requesting a slight extension. Next, the Danish envoy, the British chargé d'affaires, and the American consul also inquired with the Ministry and requested flexible handling, temporarily permitting the companies to retain their receiving and transmitting offices. After several explanations, the envoys and consuls of the United Kingdom, the United States, and Denmark expressed satisfaction. Consequently, the companies abandoned their demands and, in accordance with the original text, sent representatives to the Ministry of Transportation on (April 5) to apply for licenses and formally sign the contract with the Directorate General of Telecommunications.

Key Points of the Contract 75

The contract content was signed in accordance with the original proposal approved by the National Government. Key points are as follows: (1) Cancel the patent right for submarine cable landing. According to the old contracts signed by our country with Great Eastern and Great Northern companies during the Guangxu period, without the consent of both parties, no other party was allowed to set up a line to land or communicate in other ways within our country during the contract period. This clause has now been abolished. (2) Stipulate the time limit for submarine cable landing and regulations. The term of the previous contract of Great Eastern and Great Northern companies was 20 years, and the term of the Pacific company was 25 years. The current contract is set for 14 years, and they must apply for a license in accordance with the Commercial Submarine Cable Landing Regulations promulgated by the Ministry, and abide by all the conditions in the regulations. (3) Recover the right to directly send and receive telegrams. The current contract stipulates that the Shanghai telegraph receiving and sending offices of the companies shall be taken over and operated by the Ministry of Transportation, and they shall no longer have the right to directly send and receive telegrams. (4) Revise the line fee to be obtained by our side. For water-line telegrams passing through our country, in the past, European telegrams were divided by an average of 38.5 centimes per word, and American telegrams were divided by an average of 47 centimes per word. The current contract specifies that ordinary telegrams from Shanghai to Europe are 35 centimes per word, and from other places in China to Europe are 60 centimes per word. Telegrams from Shanghai to the Americas are 45 centimes per word, and telegrams from other places in China to the Americas are 70 centimes per word. Our country did not have any line fee for telegrams to and from Shanghai with Japan, the Philippines, the South Seas, and Hong Kong. The current contract specifies 20 centimes per word for Japan and the Philippines, 25 centimes per word for the South Seas, 4 minutes for Hong Kong Huaming, Huami and 8 minutes for foreign language. (5) Recover the underground cable and overhead lines. The underground cable and overhead lines used by the company from the submarine cable landing to its operating room were managed by the company itself. Even our country's own underground cable had to be opened by Great Northern Company. The current contract stipulates that, except for the underground cables required by the company to be borrowed during the contract period, all other cables will be taken back. (6) Recover the borrowing line from Tianjin-Gu. In the past, the land line from Tianjin to Gu was borrowed by the company for its exclusive use, and no rent was charged. The maintenance of the line had to be borne by our country. It has now been completely recovered for our own use. The Great Northern and Great Eastern newspaper rooms in Tianjin and Beijing have also been recovered by our country. (7) Cancel the Fuzhou Great Eastern Company and the Xiamen Great Northern Company. The Shanghai-Hong Kong water line of the company used to land at Fuzhou and Gulangyu respectively to set up bureaus to send and receive telegrams, which were parallel to our land line. This time it was also taken back.

Official Signing Situation 76

The two parties first sent specialists to proofread the contract and all vouchers with each other in advance, and worked hard day and night. The entire proofreading was completed on the morning of the 5th. In the afternoon at 3:00 PM, the official signing was held. Yan Renguang, Director of the Directorate General of Telecommunications of the Ministry of Transportation, was the signatory of the contract, and Guo Shiheng, the chief of the Section, was the witness. Great Eastern sent Ding Fuerden, Great Northern Peng Sheng, and Pacific Kailai, and the British, Danish and American consuls certified. At the time, they all gathered in the meeting hall of the Ministry. First, Yan Renguang, Chairman of the Ministry of Transportation, delivered a speech, followed by Peng Xing, manager of Great Northern, who answered on behalf of the three companies. Then, the contract and all vouchers were signed and sealed with each other. It was not completed until 6:00 PM.

Pessimism About the Future of the Silk Industry 80

Since Japan withdrew from the League of Nations, I am deeply afraid that countries will use the League of Nations covenant to impose economic sanctions, and the domestic economy is extremely panic. Therefore, Japanese silk has plummeted in price in European and American markets, and is being dumped in order to absorb cash. As a result, no one asks about Chinese silk. It has completely stopped in the United States. Even in the market, calculated according to Japanese silk, each tan (unit of weight) is only more than 460 taels. Although there is some trading in France, the price is also less than 600 taels. As for the users of silk, the domestic silk factories, firstly, are wary because of the sharp drop in the foreign silk market, and secondly, because of the extremely tight silver, the silk sales are stagnant, so they all take a wait-and-see attitude. The price is only slightly more than 100 taels, and there are very few transactions. A few days ago, only the Suzhou silk factory purchased three tan (unit of weight) of warp silk from the Dechang silk factory, without any large transactions. It is expected that the price of spring cocoons will be difficult to improve, and the future of the rural economy will become more and more pessimistic.

It was decided to allow the sale of domestic species in various counties and postpone the crackdown, and immediately send Secretary Li Yu to post notices and persuade shops to open in order to avoid expanding the situation, and order the provincial committee and the county government to discuss solutions for handling the aftermath.

Shang Zhen's Representative Cheng Qilu Talks About the Battle of Lengkou 87

"As Long as There is a Breath, I Will Never Allow the Enemy to Cross the Line!"

"The Alert Line Has Been Extended to More Than Twenty Li Outside the Pass"

Shanghai Times Electric News Agency Local News: Shang Zhen, the representative of the Second Army Corps of North China, Mr. Cheng Qilu, just returned from the battlefield. He personally witnessed the bloody battle of Lengkou. Because the public has been informed of the army's battle and defense situation, the detailed situation is still vague. He arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the previous day and planned to report to the local associations and other groups about the bloody battle of Lengkou. A reporter from the Shanghai Times News Agency visited his residence. He was kindly received and told the details of the army's battle. Details are described below.

Current Strength of the Army 88

According to Mr. Cheng, the army has three divisions, Huang Guanghua, Gao Hongwen, and Li Xingcun. Friendly troops under his command include He Zhuguo's unit of more than 10,000 people and Gao Guizi's unit of ☐☐ people, totaling more than ☐ 10,000 people. However, transportation equipment such as military telephones, trucks, steel helmets, and large knives are very lacking.

The Loss of Lengkou 89

Lengkou is the right wing of the entire North China line and an important passage to Pingjin. If Lengkou is lost, Pingjin will be threatened. At the same time, Gubeikou on the left wing and Xifengkou on the front will be in danger of being encircled. Therefore, Lengkou also occupies an important position in this military operation. After Chengde was lost, Lengkou also fell. Shang General Commander had been ordered by the Military Branch Association to take charge of the right wing. After hearing the news of the fall of Lengkou on the 4th, he ordered the Huang Guanghua Division of the army to advance north as soon as possible and arrive near Lengkou on the 6th. The enemy had increased from more than 200 people to more than 1,000 people. Armored vehicles had increased from more than a dozen to dozens, mixed with puppet army infantry and artillery units, and built a solid position in an attempt to hold the Lengkou pass.

Bloody Battle to Recapture Lengkou 90

At dawn on the 7th, our army ordered a counterattack on the enemy's position. The enemy resisted stubbornly, but our army was tragic and excited, and its spirit was multiplied. They took risks and charged. More than a dozen enemy armored vehicles were destroyed at the time, and the enemy's casualties were countless. It was not until 5:00 PM on the same day that the enemy could not support it and collapsed and retreated to the outside of the pass. The Huang Division, except for a part that remained to defend the recaptured Lengkou pass, the rest rushed out of the pass and pursued the victory. The enemy's reinforcements also arrived from the rear. The army resisted on one side and engaged in defense work on the other. The alert line was set up in Xiaojiaying and Madaogou.

Enemy Stubborn Resistance 91

On the evening of the 21st, the enemy transferred four mixed detachments from Xifengkou and Gubeikou, and fierce battles were fought at the above locations. The position was gained and lost, and lost and regained, more than a dozen times. The enemy's momentum weakened slightly, and our army rushed out of the trenches. The enemy collapsed to the north. The enemy's corpses and dead horses blocked the road. After Lengkou was recaptured, the rear of Luanping was greatly consolidated. However, the peaks more than 20 miles outside the pass are still in the hands of the enemy. However, the enemy is determined to coexist and die with Lengkou. As long as there is a breath, the enemy will never be allowed to cross the line. According to the latest news, there will be a detailed telegram report within the day. However, the soldiers on the front line are using their lives to kill the enemy. The rear hopes that the whole country will be united in order to win the final victory.

Factory Inspection Promotes Concessions

Police Reform Difficult to Implement Immediately

Preparation for Collecting Land Value Tax Completed

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Mr. Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, yesterday and asked him about various issues related to municipal facilities. He was told as follows:

Factory Inspection 94

According to Mr. Yu, after repeated consultations with Mr. Feixin Dun, President of the Municipal Council, regarding factory inspection, he can agree to our assistance. However, in terms of methods, he requires us to send trained inspection talents to be controlled by the concession side. However, the Factory Law was promulgated by the National Government, and the Municipal Government was ordered to implement it. This kind of requirement actually hinders our administrative power. Moreover, the citizens of the concession naturally comply with the orders of the Chinese government and are protected by the Chinese government. Therefore, the administrative power of the Chinese government can naturally be implemented in the concession, so that the Chinese and concession areas are treated equally. Therefore, there is no considerable result. According to the concession authorities, this issue will be handled in the amendment of the Yangjingbang Regulations at the annual meeting of Western taxpayers in this session. However, the Yangjingbang Regulations also clearly stipulate that the amendment of the articles must also be agreed to by the Chinese government before it can take effect.

Police System 95

The reform of the police system, former Director Wen had this proposal, but it was not implemented due to the winter defense period. This is because the various districts of Zhabei are busy with reorganization and revival, and at the same time, they want to enrich the police force and increase training efforts. The reform can be implemented only after these two tasks are completed. As for the relocation of the Public Security Bureau to the old Shanghai County site, because the county site is currently being renovated, it will probably take some time.

Tax Revenue 96

After the Director of the Finance Bureau negotiated with the concession authorities on entertainment donations, there has been no considerable result, so it is still difficult to collect. The business tax is in suspension. The preparations for collecting land value tax have been completed. The date of collection has not yet been determined, but it will be realized soon.

Revival Situation 97

Since the allocation of funds for the plan to revive the prosperity of this city, it has been actively carried out. The construction of trunk roads, as well as the municipal library and hospital, have all been implemented in order, and the progress is quite rapid. In the city center area, the municipal government building and various trunk roads will also be completed separately. However, the entire project must be completed by the end of this year. Therefore, although the relocation of the municipal government agencies was possible in mid-July, it should be at the end of the year based on actual observation.

Western Merchants Also Gradually Comply with Abolishing Taels and Changing to Yuan 99

The Great American Evening News said that regarding the abolition of taels and the change to yuan, in addition to the Chinese banks deciding to change all the tael accounts to yuan accounts according to the fixed rate, the latest progress of the Western merchants is as follows: (1) HSBC Bank has decided that from next week, all foreign exchange rates will be calculated in silver yuan, such as how many pence can be exchanged for one yuan of national currency, how many cents for US dollars, how many francs for French francs, and how many marks for German marks; (2) The Shanghai Western Merchants Exchange Association has discussed the policy of agreement and unified action, but has not yet issued a formal statement; (3) The London Stock Exchange no longer quotes in taels; (4) A large number of cargo contracts in this port have been changed from taels to silver yuan according to the fixed rate; (5) Western merchants have discussed the issue that contracts in taels will not be accepted by the court in the future. In addition, it is also confirmed that the pattern of the new national currency will also be slightly changed, but the weight and fineness will be absolutely unaffected according to the legal standard.

The Failure of Yoshizawa's Visit to China 100

Scheduled to Depart Shanghai Northward Today

Departure Not Intended as Negative Report on China

The Great American Evening Post reports that former Japanese Foreign Minister Yoshizawa, in a conversation with representatives of foreign newspapers in Shanghai today (the 7th), stated that his visit to Shanghai was purely of a personal nature. Claims in Chinese newspapers that he was charged with direct negotiations with the Chinese government were entirely baseless. He mentioned that he had been away from Shanghai for four years and was visiting to experience the atmosphere of central China and to observe everything on the ground. He did not bear any formal or semi-formal mission. He is scheduled to travel north to Tianjin and Beijing tomorrow (the 8th), and then proceed to Manchuria for a week before returning to Tokyo. His purpose in visiting Manchuria is to investigate the development of "that country." When asked about his opinion on the Four-Power Agreement, Yoshizawa replied that British Prime Minister MacDonald's efforts seemed to have succeeded. However, since the British Prime Minister announced the progress of the matter in the House of Commons, Japan has not heard of any further developments. It is said that the agreement has been shelved due to France's attitude. When questioned about his views on disarmament, Yoshizawa responded that although the Disarmament Conference still exists and Japanese representatives still participate in its meetings, the atmosphere is not very promising. Although Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, it will continue to cooperate with the major powers to maintain world peace. While the future is uncertain, it appears that the Japanese government's policy will not deviate from cooperation with the major powers. The discussion then turned to the Chinese boycott of Japanese goods. Yoshizawa said that even if the boycott movement intensifies, the Japanese government will not take any special actions. However, if Chinese actions become excessive and cause unexpected incidents or violence, he is certain that the Japanese government will take appropriate measures. The boycott movement is a matter of serious concern for the Japanese government, and it will take measures to deal with it if necessary. Finally, regarding the Philippine Islands issue, Yoshizawa replied with a smile that the independence of the Philippine Islands is not Japan's concern at all.

Shanghai, Wuhan, Tianjin, and Wuxi Chinese Cotton Mills to Hold Regular Meetings to Discuss Production Reduction Measures 104

Reason Being Forced by Overproduction

Xin Sheng She reports that there has been talk recently of Shanghai cotton mills collectively discussing production reduction measures. A Xin Sheng She reporter, considering cotton yarn to be China's largest industry and the implications of a sudden reduction in production to be far-reaching, visited a leader in the cotton industry to inquire about the situation and the reasons for the reduction. The leader provided a detailed explanation, stating that in the past two years, all industries in the country have been declining. The reasons are, on the one hand, the global economic recession, overproduction, and efforts to promote foreign trade. China's low tariffs have resulted in a dumping ground for foreign goods. This is how Chinese industries are experiencing the pain of the global economic recession. On the other hand, there are reasons specific to China itself. Since the massive floods in the Yangtze River basin in 1931, banditry has spread, and the rural economy is on the verge of collapse. Purchasing power has greatly decreased, and the sales of all goods are less than half of what they were in the past. The September 18th and January 28th incidents followed, and the national financial situation was greatly affected, severely impacting industry. The cotton yarn industry, as China's largest industry, is experiencing even greater pain than other industries. This is because, in addition to Chinese merchants, there are also foreign cotton mills in the country, with spindles almost equal in number to those of Chinese mills. This is unique to the cotton industry and a hardship not shared by other industries. The raw material for cotton mills is cotton. Domestic cotton production, both in terms of quality and quantity, cannot meet demand, and prices are too high. Leaving aside the distant past, in 1931, the lowest price for standard yarn was 145 taels and 2 mace, and the lowest price for standard cotton was 30 taels, 3 mace, and 5 fen. In 1932, the lowest price for standard yarn was 138 taels and 3 mace, and standard cotton was 27 taels. This year, in March, the lowest market price for standard yarn was 132 taels and 6 mace, and standard cotton was 30 taels and 7 mace and 5 fen. Comparing this year with 1932, the price of yarn has fallen by 5 taels and 7 mace, while the price of cotton has risen by 3 taels and 7 mace and 5 fen. Compared with 1931 (the standard for yarn and cotton in 1933 was different from that in 1931; if the 1933 standard is converted to the equivalent of the 1931 standard, the standard would be 120 taels and 6 mace, and the standard cotton would be approximately 29 taels), the price of cotton yarn has fallen by 24 taels and 6 mace, while the price of cotton has risen by 2 taels. From this simple comparison of prices, it is clear what the trend of yarn and cotton prices has been in the past two years and how the cotton mills are operating. This is from the perspective of raw materials. Now, let's talk about the sales of finished products. Under the current domestic economic situation, the sales of all goods are sluggish, but cotton yarn is particularly so. China imports the most cotton goods, as anyone familiar with the customs trade situation knows. Secondly, foreign mills account for almost half of the spindles in the country, and the yarn and cloth they produce are naturally sold domestically. This is an external competition that is unique to the cotton mills. Since the September 18th Incident, the sales of yarn and cloth in the three northeastern provinces have been completely occupied by Japanese domestic goods. Increasingly, new yarn and cloth made by Japanese factories in China are being shipped to northern China due to strict restrictions on goods in southern China and the Yangtze River. Therefore, before long, Chinese-owned yarn and cloth factories in northern China will have no room to gain a foothold, eventually forcing yarn from Tianjin and Shanxi factories to be shipped south. This is a rare phenomenon in the past, and Shanghai is feeling the sluggish sales even more. Since last summer, Japanese factories have been using dumping tactics in northern China and have seen success. They are now promoting this tactic in the Yangtze River region. Therefore, since last winter, yarn sales in the Yangtze River region have gradually decreased, and the inventory of yarn in Shanghai has been increasing month by month, reaching a massive 140,000 to 150,000 bales. This has forced the discussion of production reduction measures. It is now proposed to stop production for two or three days each week, reducing the original production by about one-third, to reduce production and better match consumption. This is because the factory owners are thinking of the workers and are making the minimum possible reduction in production, hoping that the environment will improve. If they do not seek to maintain the current situation and allow the current deteriorating situation to continue, it will soon be worse than reducing production by one-third. At that time, what will be the plight of the workers? It seems that Shanghai cotton mills have already decided to reduce production. It is reported that the Cotton Mill Association will hold a general membership meeting on the 10th, bringing together factories from Shanghai, Wuhan, Tianjin, and Wuxi to jointly decide on and implement the measures uniformly. All the details of the production reduction measures are still to be decided at the meeting on the 10th.

○　　○　　○　　○

British Chamber of Commerce Annual Meeting Report 105

Commercial Counsellor Peel's Speech

British Goods Imports Still Maintain Old Status

Trust in China's Great Future

The North China Daily News reports that at yesterday's (6th) annual meeting of the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai, British Commercial Counsellor Peel gave a speech, in which he stated the following regarding Sino-foreign trade: Last year was difficult to compare with previous years due to the Manchurian problem. In 1931, Manchurian exports accounted for 35% of the total national exports, while its imports only accounted for 10% to 11% of the national total. However, from our perspective, the brightest point last year was that imports of British goods were still able to maintain their old status, with no decrease of even a penny compared to 1931. On the contrary, our major competitors all saw sharp declines, such as the United States, which decreased by no less than 92 million Haikwan taels, France by 8 million taels, and Germany by 12 million taels. Moreover, in the major imported goods, such as cotton textiles, British goods saw an increase. Furthermore, the British goods that can compete with other countries in China's import trade are all manufactured goods. Considering the total amount of manufactured goods imported into China this year, Britain accounted for no less than 24%, a large increase over the previous year. Also, in 1931, the value of British goods imported accounted for just over 8% of the total value of imports into China, while last year it accounted for 11.5%, an increase of no less than 40% compared to the previous year. According to last year's customs report, the value of goods imported from the United States ranked first, but 80% of these were food and raw materials. In terms of manufactured goods, the value of British imports was twice that of the United States. Peel also stated that last year, China experienced an even more significant phenomenon: the ability of its people to withstand all kinds of terrible blows, such as the occupation of Manchuria, the Shanghai Incident, and major floods. In his view, China has a great future. He has deep trust not only in China's future but also in the future of the world. He believes that the responsibility of the British lies in working with other nations to resolutely advance towards reason and progress, for the benefit of others, and that they will also gain great glory. China's greatest need today lies in clearing debts and restoring credit. If it does not focus on these two goals, it will not be able to achieve great development. However, he believes that those in power are currently paying sincere attention to this. In his address, Chairman Marshall first described the impact of China's foreign troubles and internal worries, and its ability to still balance its budget. He then analyzed the Sino-foreign trade situation last year, stating that the United States ranked first in Sino-foreign trade, accounting for 21.16%, Japan ranked second, accounting for 17.07%, Britain ranked third, accounting for 10.07%, and Hong Kong ranked fourth, accounting for 8.71%. However, a large part of Hong Kong's trade with China naturally represents Sino-British trade. He then discussed the Ministry of Railways' clearing of debts and progress in railway construction, the new regulations of the customs requiring imported goods to be labelled with the country of origin in Chinese characters, the purchasing power of the Chinese people, and the construction of roads, disaster relief, and the development of transportation facilities. Regarding China's commerce and industry, we must know that the area of this country is almost like a continent, and the population is large, but the average wealth per person is very small. Therefore, its material progress, when compared with its area and population, is slow. But when compared with the average wealth per person, it is not so slow. On the same day, after passing the report and re-electing new directors, the meeting adjourned and the annual meeting of the British Community in China Association was convened.

Sun Ke and Others Arrive in Shanghai This Morning 106

Sun Ke, Li Shizeng, Chen Gongbo, Zhu Jiahua, Ma Chaojun, Liang Hancao, Chuan Bingchang, and others left Beijing together on the Beijing-Shanghai night train at 11:30 last night and are expected to arrive in Shanghai at around 8:00 this morning.

Dai Yongtang, Director of the Fishery Construction Fee Collection Office, Assumes Office 107

Collection Scheduled to Begin on April 15th

Also Discusses the Relationship Between Fee Collection and Fishermen

The Industry Ministry's Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Improvement Committee has established an office to collect fishery construction fees and has resolved to have Committee Member Dai Yongtang concurrently serve as Director of the Collection Office, as previously reported. It has now been learned that since being appointed, Dai has been actively preparing and deploying everything. He has divided the important production and sales locations within the Jiangsu-Zhejiang region into ten districts, and officially began work on the morning of the 6th, announcing the start of operations. The collection office is located in Changan Lane on Huangjia Que Road in Xiaoximen. Dai also spoke about the circumstances surrounding the establishment of the office by the Industry Ministry's Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Improvement Committee to collect fishery construction fees, in accordance with the resolution of the Central Political Conference. The process has been very difficult. It has now been decided that the construction fee will begin to be collected on April 15th. Fearing that various sectors may not yet understand the truth, he is publishing the circumstances as follows: Last year, foreign vessels were encroaching on our fishing grounds with increasing urgency. In order to reorganize the domestic fishing industry, it was originally planned to collect a fishery product tax of 5% of the value, according to the Fishery Law. Our fishing industry felt deeply that it could not afford to increase the burden at this time of decline in the fishing industry. Therefore, various Jiangsu and Zhejiang fishing groups united to form a Tax Exemption Committee, showing their collective opposition. Since then, letters and telegrams have been exchanged, repeatedly requesting the central government to maintain the original tax exemption order. Later, after Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry traveled back and forth between Beijing and Shanghai, and engaged in several sincere consultations with fishing industry leaders, the fishery tax was reduced from 5% to 2%. Fishing industry leaders also believed that using the name "fishery tax" would inevitably lead to increases in the future. Moreover, since it was called a fishery tax, it would be one of the national tax revenues. Once collected, it might not necessarily be taken from fisheries and used for fisheries. Therefore, they unanimously requested that the collected fee be absolutely designated as a fishery construction fee and that the fishing industry have the right to manage, audit, and distribute the funds to ensure credibility. The Minister adopted these suggestions one by one, and after several careful discussions, it was decided to change the fee to a fishery construction fee of 2% of the market value of fishery products, collected once. Whether fresh, salted, dried, or shellfish, all are required to pay the construction fee to show no favoritism. Those less than 100 catties or small-scale hawkers are exempt from the fee. Once the agreement was reached, the Ministry, provincial government, municipal government, Jiangsu-Zhejiang-Shanghai fishing industry, and various experts jointly organized the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Improvement Committee to achieve the real effect of cooperation between the government and the people. Since the establishment of the Fisheries Improvement Committee, it has been ordered by the Ministry to collect the fishery construction fee. The meeting also resolved (1) that the fees collected will be used exclusively to protect the safety of the fishing industry, to manage the strictest possible ocean protection, to add ocean patrol ships, and for the necessary construction for the fishery industry. (2) Once the construction fee is collected, the ocean protection fee will be stopped altogether, and all the miscellaneous expenses that fishermen previously bore, such as various ship licenses, will be cancelled. (3) Recently, Committee Member Du Yuesheng and others proposed that, in order to reduce the burden on fishermen, the collection of the construction fee should be further reduced to 1%. In summary, our fishermen fulfill the minimum obligations and receive the greatest benefits. Anyone who understands the matter should celebrate the revival of the fishing industry, which is now dependent on this. Yongtang was erroneously promoted by the committee to the position of Director of the Collection Office. Realizing his lack of talent and heavy responsibility, he originally dared not accept. However, as a member of the fishing community, at this time of extreme decline in the fishing industry, now that the government has the determination to reorganize the fishing industry, how can our fishing community be willing to lag behind? Therefore, without considering his inadequacy, he immediately obeyed the order to prepare. The office has now been formally established, and the collection is scheduled to begin on the 15th of this month. Believing that construction depends on funding, and that small contributions can make a large coat, with every bit of financial strength, a bit of work can be done, he deeply hopes that his colleagues in the fishing industry will happily contribute, so that the various fishery improvement construction plans that we deeply expect can be carried out in an orderly manner, and then the future of the fishing industry may be hopeful.

Meat Inspection Dispute: Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram to Ministry Requesting Resolution 108

And Sends Letter to Health Bureau Requesting Storage of Detained Goods

The local ham and preserved meat industry opposes the meat inspection case. However, the Municipal Health Bureau has implemented inspections this month, resulting in the recent arrival of goods from the industry being detained and exposed at the station. Rain and wind are causing the meat products to rot. The industry specifically sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting protection. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in addition to forwarding the letter to the Municipal Health Bureau for investigation, also sent a telegram to the Industry Ministry of the Executive Yuan, requesting a prompt resolution. The original texts are recorded separately below.

Telegram to the Ministry: To the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing, The inspection of preserved meats in this city was ordered to be cancelled by your (Executive) Yuan on December 30th of last year, after a presentation from the two industry associations. Barely three months later, the Municipal Health Bureau is again setting up words to continue the operation, disregarding national laws and regulations. We have already telegraphed jointly, requesting another order to stop it, but we have not received a reply. Now, according to reports from the industry, the Health Bureau is forcibly detaining goods and accumulating them in the open air. Over time, this will likely cause them to spoil, which contradicts the stated goal of hygiene. If this matter is not resolved quickly by the Ministry, merchants will suffer huge losses in cost. Please expedite the matter urgently. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Letter to the Health Bureau: Dear Sirs, We have received a letter from the Ham Industry Association stating that the issue of forcing the cancellation of inspections has been approved by the Executive Yuan. Recently, the Municipal Health Bureau has suddenly implemented inspections, publishing a notice two days ago. As a result, the goods of our colleagues that were en route were unable to stop in time due to this bolt from the blue. Therefore, in the past two or three days, more than a hundred pieces of ham and wind-dried meat newly transported from Hangzhou have been stopped by police officers sent by the Health Bureau after arriving in Shanghai, and are piled up in the open air of the South Station, without allowing any movement. As the weather warms up, the heat of the sun is quite strong during the day. Piling them up for too long will inevitably turn these items, which were originally hygienic, into unsanitary goods. Moreover, the Municipal Health Bureau is loudly proclaiming that the implementation of meat inspection is for the sake of protecting the health of meat-eating citizens. If this is the case, does it not greatly contradict what they say? Moreover, the requests for cancellation made by the association have been made from the standpoint of law and reason. Even if the Health Bureau is determined to achieve its goal of inspection and fee collection, it should also be reasonable to follow legal procedures. Today, instead of doing so, they are forcing the goods arriving at the station to be piled up in the open air. There is nothing more vicious than this method. Considering the future of the industry and the national legislation, our industry is determined not to accept any inspection or payment of fees before the case has been properly determined. However, the value of the goods that have arrived is very large, so we have no choice but to report the situation. We hope that you will uphold the principle of protecting commerce and contact the Municipal Health Bureau to first have the shipping company that handled the goods transport and store them properly to avoid unexpected events. This is in the public interest. We have found that the officials and merchants in this city are still disputing over the implementation of meat inspection. How it will be resolved in the future should be awaited. However, before the Executive Yuan issues a clear order, the official should not impose restrictions on the business activities of the industry. The request in the letter, before the case has been properly resolved, that even if the industry's meat products must be detained due to not accepting inspection and payment of fees, they should be stored properly in a selected location to avoid the meat products from being exposed to the sun and becoming easily rotten, is a legitimate request. We are sending you a letter requesting that you investigate and allow the shipping company handling the obstructed meat products in the open air to transport and store them properly to alleviate the merchants' difficulties.

Government Measures to Rescue the Silk Industry 110

Plans Relief Based on On-Site Investigations

Mr. Song Ziwen, Vice Chairman of the National Economic Commission, realizing that China's silk industry is on the verge of extinction and must be rescued, specifically assigned commissioners in the past few months to go to the silk regions of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to conduct on-site investigations and thorough research. Based on the results of the investigation and research, he formulated a rescue plan that includes solutions to various problems such as mulberry planting, seed production, silkworm cocoon sales, silk reeling, and maintaining silk factories. It is reported that experiments on crossbred silkworm rearing will be started at the Hangzhou Women's Sericulture School, and model silkworm farming experimental areas will be established in Xiaoshan and Jintan counties to test the silkworm varieties for suitability to the Chinese climate and the capabilities of the silkworm farmers, and whether the resulting silkworm cocoons can indeed increase silk production. More than ninety guidance centers will be set up in the Xiaoshan and Jintan experimental areas, each with a silkworm rearing room and a baking room, until the end of the second molt. The number of silkworm eggs to be tested is estimated to be more than 23,000 sheets, and the number of farmers who will be influenced and gain experience in rearing their young silkworms with good methods is estimated to be more than 27,000 households, which is quite staggering. However, it is said that the government will not stop there, but plans to use the two experimental areas as a starting point to gradually expand to the whole country, and will not stop until the Chinese silk industry has restored its position in the world market. It is also reported that the funds for the implementation of the preliminary plan have all been raised.

Yan Fuqing Discusses the Situation of Frontline Medical Relief 111

丨Very Organized丨

Yan Fuqing, President of the National Shanghai Medical College and concurrently President of the First Hospital of the Chinese Red Cross Society, previously, due to the urgency of the war in North China and the need to care for wounded soldiers, led more than twenty physicians and medical students from the college to Peiping in mid-July. They organized a hospital for wounded soldiers, which is now ready. Mr. Yan returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday to handle hospital affairs and made the following statement: This time, the organization of medical relief work in the North is very orderly, with the North China Relief Committee as the backbone. The committee is composed of fourteen medical leaders, with Liu Ruiheng as Director and myself and Jiang Tiren as Deputy Directors. A total of 150 volunteer medical personnel were sent by major medical institutions in the country, including forty from Peiping Union Medical College, twenty-one from National Shanghai Medical College, ten from National Peiping University Medical College, twenty from Qilu University Medical College, twelve from Xiangya Medical College, and others from Central Hospital and the Ministry of Health. Medical circles in various places are also preparing to mobilize, and they can set off as soon as needed. In this war, the total number of wounded soldiers in Rehe and North China is six to seven thousand, of whom five thousand have been accommodated in the battlefield and rear hospitals established by the Committee. To facilitate the reception of wounded soldiers from outside the pass, the Committee has established wounded soldier hospitals at Xifengkou, Gubeikou, and Duolun in Peiping. The three hospitals in Zunhua, Miyun, and Kangzhuang are all equipped with ambulance teams, with medicines for treatment prepared in the vehicles, rushing to the front line for transport. Two rear hospitals are set up in Peiping, one in Shifuyuan and one in Feng Yong University. The above two can accommodate 1,300 seriously wounded soldiers. In addition, a rear hospital is set up in Tongzhou, specializing in severely wounded soldiers. The above three are central coordinating agencies for rescue and treatment, sending those with severe injuries and light injuries to hospitals set up by the Military Medical Directorate along the Jinpu Railway. In addition to working hard to rescue, the Committee also provides medical supplies to wounded soldier hospitals in various places, and within its possible range, sends doctors and nurses to assist the hospitals established by the Military Medical Directorate. In short, the relief work this time is well-organized, does not cost much money, and has achieved great results. The spirit of the people who report their services from all over the place is excellent.

Prohibition of 100-Ton Ships for Sea Transportation 117

Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Berlecht, Chief Secretary, jointly issued a notice yesterday, stating that to jointly issue a notice, it is found that ships or steamers registered under one hundred tons are not allowed to directly engage in business between domestic and foreign ports. In addition, since September 25th, 21st year of the Republic of China, the customs of the three northeastern provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang have been temporarily closed, and the measures for changing the treatment of domestic navigation of civilian ships and between Dalian, Niuzhuang, and Andong have been announced by the undersigned on January 28th, September 23rd, and October 24th of the 20th and 21st years of the Republic of China. Now, according to the government's order, hereinafter, all ships and steamers registered under one hundred tons are not allowed to directly engage in business between domestic ports and the ports of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang provinces and Dalian. Upon receiving this, all shipping merchants are to be informed. This notice is hereby issued.

Zhengji Guangli Ship and Japanese Ship Collide in Fog at Jiming Island 118

Both Ships Damaged, Japanese Ship Taking on Water

Crew Members Board Guangli and Tow Back to Weihaiwei

The Zhengji Shipping Company's Guangli ship departed from Qingdao to Dalian the day before yesterday, carrying passengers and cargo. When sailing near Jiming Island east of Weihaiwei, it encountered heavy fog and collided with the Japanese ship Kyodo Maru No. 36. Both ships were damaged. The details are as follows:

Collision in Fog 119

The Zhengji Company's head office is in Yingkou, and a branch is located on Tianzhutang Street in the French Concession of Shanghai. The Guangli ship is a miscellaneous ship (commonly known as a "wild chicken ship"), specializing in carrying passengers and cargo, sailing to Niuzhuang, Qingdao, Fujian, Shanghai, and other places, with a deadweight of 1,200 tons. It departed from Qingdao the day before yesterday, carrying cargo to Dalian. At about 4:00 PM on the sixth, when it was sailing to Jiming Island about eighteen miles east of Weihaiwei, it encountered heavy fog and collided with the Japanese ship Kyodo Maru No. 36, which was sailing from Weihaiwei to Incheon, Korea.

Various Damages 120

The iron and nails on the bow of the Guangli ship were damaged. A large hole was punched in the engine room on the port side of the Japanese ship, seawater entered, and the machinery was damaged by the water, making it impossible to sail. The Guangli ship immediately took rescue measures, transferring all the crew members and passengers of the Japanese ship to the Guangli. At the same time, they checked the damaged part of the Japanese ship and learned that it would not sink.

Towed Back to Weihaiwei 121

At that time, efforts were quickly made to block the damaged part of the engine room of the Japanese ship to prevent seawater from entering. At the same time, the Guangli ship towed the Japanese ship to Weihaiwei for berthing. The Japanese ship has now entered the dock for repairs. The Guangli ship decided to sail to Dalian before repairing.

Insurance Dispute over the Jianhua Factory, the Center of the January 28th Front Line in Northeast China 122

丨Zhang Shenzhi Accuses Xie Ruisen of Embezzling Insurance Money丨

The Jianhua Shenji Textile Factory was originally opened on Tiantong'an Road in Zhabei. During the January 28th incident, when the Japanese invaded Shanghai, the factory was located at the center of the front line. Its manager, Zhang Shenzhi, at the time, because the factory's machinery, wealth, and goods were worth more than 100,000 taels of gold, in order to protect the property, took out a war risk insurance policy for 100,000 taels of silver with Xie Ruisen, manager of the Baoxing Insurance Company on the upper floor of the HSBC Bank on Fuzhou Road, on the day after the outbreak of the war (January 29th). It was divided into two types: (1) 70,000 taels for machinery, (2) 30,000 taels for goods, with a term of one month and an insurance premium of 3,000 taels of silver. On the same day, Xie gave Zhang two insurance policies. After Zhang reviewed them, he learned that Xie was reinsuring with Dechang Company, so the insurance policies were issued by Dechang. Zhang believed that this kind of reinsurance was common in the insurance industry, so he did not object and immediately paid a draft from Yuanda Bank for 3,000 taels. On February 5th, when Yuanda opened for business, Xie entrusted the draft to Hengxun Bank for encashment. On the 19th of that month, Zhang learned that the Jianhua Factory had been bombed by Japanese planes and immediately informed Xie Ruisen and asked whether a written report was needed. Xie replied that a written report was not needed and that he would forward the information to Dechang, the insurer. However, after the Japanese planes began bombing the factory on the 19th, they did not stop, and the entire factory was destroyed in three days. Zhang also continued to inform Xie of the tragic situation. Unexpectedly, Xie suddenly sent a letter to Zhang, stating that Dechang Company, the insurer, had declared its withdrawal from insurance to him as early as February 2nd, and that he had also notified Zhang by letter the day after Dechang's withdrawal, so he was no longer responsible for the insurance. Zhang was shocked upon receiving the letter and has been negotiating with Xie ever since, for more than a year. Not only has he not received any compensation for his losses, but the 3,000 taels of insurance premium he paid has also been thrown into a bottomless pit. Now, he has hired lawyer E Sen to file a criminal self-accusation against Xie Ruisen for embezzling the draft, stating that the defendant's claim that he had notified the withdrawal of insurance by letter on February 3rd is entirely fabricated. If that were the case, why did the defendant still take the insurance premium draft he paid to the bank for encashment on February 5th? And when Zhang sent personnel and a letter to inform him of the damage to the factory site on February 19th, why was there no declaration of withdrawal? Since Dechang had withdrawn insurance from the defendant, the defendant should have notified the plaintiff and returned the 3,000 taels of insurance premium. However, the defendant did not do this, but instead cashed the draft and concealed the fact that Dechang had declared its withdrawal, which was obviously an intentional embezzlement of the insurance premium and violated the provisions of Article 356 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, he has filed a lawsuit requesting the arrest of the defendant and to be punished according to the law. Due to the defendant's illegal embezzlement and concealment of facts, the plaintiff has suffered losses and hereby files a civil lawsuit as an attachment. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan of the First Special District Local Court held a hearing, but the defendant was absent. His lawyer claimed that the defendant had left Shanghai for business and requested a postponement. However, the plaintiff's lawyer, E Sen, stated that the defendant had been appointed as the director of the Insurance Department of the Four Banks' Reserve Treasury yesterday and would not have left Shanghai, so his lawyer's statement was not credible. The court then ruled that the defendant had formally requested a postponement in advance and granted the request, adjourning the hearing to the afternoon of April 25th.

Cheap National Goods Store 124

Founding Manifesto

The Shanghai National Goods Trading Company, which recently moved to the corner of Nanjing Road and Shilu, recently established a cheap national goods market at its new location on the corner of Nanjing Road and Shilu to assist national goods factories affected by the war in selling their inventory, circulate capital, seek progress in craftsmanship, and sell their products at low prices, thereby expanding business promotion. If we want to preserve peace, uphold alliances, and aid the loving troops who are hacking and slashing in the front line, we must unanimously attack the grain platform that aids the enemy troops. The purpose of our founding of the cheap national goods market is, in addition to resisting the dumping of counterfeit Japanese goods, to make the most lively location on Nanjing Road available to national goods factories that have not set up retail departments or have retail locations in remote areas. All factories that have too much inventory due to the impact of the war can entrust their inventory to be sold at low prices, or factories that are striving to promote new goods can entrust their new goods to be promoted at low prices. There are separate regulations for the entrustment methods. We hope that all national goods factories will stand on the front line of attacking the grain platform that aids the enemy and use the spirit of sacrifice of low-price sales to resist the policy of dumping counterfeit goods by treacherous merchants, in order to expand the propaganda of national goods that are truly useful.
