George Raft's Reversal of the Female Crowd (Part Two) 311

— Xi Rong

After the death of Rudolph Valentino

One of the most sought after by women

Raft was once almost raped by a crazy woman. That erotic woman used the guise of a radio announcer to meet Raft. At that time, Raft was already going to sleep, so he put on his pajamas and came out to see her. Unexpectedly, after the woman entered the room, she suddenly took off her clothes and ran towards Raft, demanding to have sex with him. Raft quickly grabbed a chair as a means of self-defense. Later, he called in his secretary to persuade the woman to leave.

Raft was first troubled by a woman in New Orleans. At that time, a young girl sneaked into Raft's dressing room in the theater. As soon as she entered, she saw Raft and demanded to kiss him. Some people also wrote to him, asking to meet him, otherwise they would commit suicide. Once it was very interesting, a pair of sisters managed to sneak into Raft's dressing room. One of the two women was only seventeen or eighteen years old, and the other was still a child. Unexpectedly, after they talked for a few minutes, the younger one suddenly shouted, "Hurry up and hold me in your arms, it's okay if you hurt me." Raft said, "Your sister is next to you. How dare I?" Unexpectedly, the sister actually said, "It doesn't matter, she's telling you to hurt her, so you hurt her." Raft knew that this pair of women was not easy to deal with either, so he tried to call his secretary to help him out. Things like this are really too numerous to mention. Fortunately, his secretary never left his side. Otherwise, Raft would have been unthinkable.

Raft said, "Married women are the most dangerous." He said, "Any married woman who can abandon her husband to seek another man, is capable of doing anything." Once a woman bribed the hotel manager and booked a room next to Raft's. When Raft went out to perform, she secretly opened his door and quietly entered his room. When Raft finished performing and came back, he saw a woman sleeping in his bed, so he picked her up, sent her out the door, locked the door himself, and went to sleep.

In addition, there were many women who made strange demands on him. Some took off their clothes and asked him to sign their vests; some asked him to draw on their lips; some asked him to kiss her shoulder, and then soak the place he kissed in red as a lifelong souvenir. There was also a wealthy widow in New York who was willing to give him a large house, as long as he lived with her for one month each year. That wealthy widow was very famous in society, and if her name was announced, it would be guaranteed to become a national sensation.

The equipment and furnishings in the theater were damaged due to women invading Raft, which was also a major loss for the theater, but the theater owners took pride in it and were not stingy at all, and asked him to come again. There were also many theaters with poor business that asked him to come once to bring good luck, and the business would be better.

Finally, Raft also has three diamond rings that were thrown on the stage by women: he wants to know their names and addresses so that he can return the rings. (End)

Film Commentary

Review of Nagana 312

— Wanshi

This is indeed a very troublesome problem. When the entire market is declining day by day, if the products of the shadow department still have to try their best to save its business crisis, then it is necessary to find another way and use all methods to find a "way out." But what new tricks are there? Love tricks are not very fashionable anymore, and thighs and sensuality are gradually becoming tiresome. Although beast films were popular for a while, they are almost a thing of the past, and everything is not very prosperous. But in the midst of no solution, we still have to think of a solution, and that is to gather these relatively new methods together to become something that is both love and sensuality, and also has the fighting of wild animals. Then "Nagana" attempts to create a style in such a purpose.

Under such deformed conditions, the screenwriter, in order to have intense scenes of beast fighting, had to reduce many of the love scenes, and the so-called sensuality had to be fulfilled with the black nudity of African natives, plus some hugs and Kisses. Because all aspects had to be taken care of, the result was that no aspect was taken care of completely.

The story of this film is extremely far-fetched: If the doctor is said to have ventured into the interior for humanitarian reasons to treat the natives, but later he did not hesitate to burn villages and release wild beasts to devour the villagers in order to save his lover from danger. According to the story, the Countess is a prostitute, but later she gave in because she could not bear the "pain of lovesickness" for the doctor; not only was there no "middle-of-the-road danger" as in the story, but also in terms of the woman herself, the character was different before and after. I don't know what kind of woman the Countess is at all? Basically, this countess and that other doctor, Stark, have no need to appear in the play. If there must be a story, then such a bizarre and far-fetched narrative that cannot justify itself really makes people feel that American films are becoming more and more hopeless. In terms of performance skills, the photography and lighting are still worth seeing. For example, the beauty of the leaf pattern at the beginning, and the stripes of shadows shown on the screen by the sunlight shining in from the blinds, are all very worth learning. The sound recording is also clear.

The director of this film can be said to have failed. Although the use of the lens was very clever at the beginning. At the same time, when the doctor went to see the Countess, he first came with a delicate voice, like the "reverse board" in this play, to increase the audience's attention to her. Like this kind of emphasis on the female role, she should be given a particularly vivid description, such as becoming a prostitute as described in the manual, but after that she was let go. Especially about her love run, it is simply not described at all, which really makes us confused. Also, the repetition of the woman's terror when she was about to be executed, because it was too repetitive, was not tense but not tense at all.

As for the actors, except for the doctor who can be compared, the rest are mediocre. Especially that woman simply can't act.

Review of "Storm Over Asia" 313

— Ling He

Poetry-like sentiment

Novel-like description

Before this article, I feel that it is necessary to say a few words about the title. Although I can't tell the reader how the original title of this film was written, judging from the English translation "Storm Over Asia" and the Japanese translation "Asian Storm", we know that it should be translated as "Asian Storm", although it is not very smooth, but it is definitely not as ambiguous as "Asian Situation". Secondly, this film was once translated as "National Soul", but it has now been remade, and a flag with a blue sky and white sun has been added to the back, tuned like the resurrection of "National Soul".

Everyone knows that this is a world-class film in Soviet films, and also the representative of the famous director Pudovkin. Of course, we do not blindly praise it because of this, but should engage in strict criticism of the work itself. Then, naturally, not only is its intention to represent the voice of the oppressed people, but also in the directing technique, there are many vigorous and very powerful types. Pudovkin is able to express the spirit of resistance of the weak nations in his works.

The Mongolian people, a weak nation, had to sell the animal skins they had worked so hard to get because of disease and for their own survival. However, they are often manipulated in the commercial monopoly of imperialism, so a silver fox can only get a very small price. However, this silver fox is the best gift that the merchant with weapons gives to the commander's lady, although it was plundered from the Mongolian people. They not only plunder in commerce, but also must use force to eliminate the resistance movement of the Mongols in order to suppress the colonies. At the same time, they use their superstition to win over and anesthetize the rulers of the colonies. Not only that, but they also try to take advantage of the feudal forces of the "Son of Heaven" to become a tool for ruling the colonies. In particular, the drama gives a detailed explanation of the imperialists' playing of puppets and the so-called "mutual respect for the interests of both sides" dog-fart treaty. As for their killing and seizing of the Mongolian people, it is simply like a daily meal. But the people of the colonies are finally resisting, and the outbreak of this resistance is, after all, like a storm that destroys imperialism. We see that this is the only way out for the oppressed people, they can only liberate themselves in the vast struggle.

Because of the director's delicate and non-greasy description, the whole rigid evolution is like a skillfully skilled novel. In the part describing the direct revolution in the back, it is like a passionate and powerful poem, even in the static picture, we can hear the tragic roar of thousands of horses galloping.

However, because the director is too focused on the protagonist, he is written as a revolutionary hero. At the same time, it is probably due to the Chinese editing, the latter part is relatively sudden and not very coherent, and the ending is too symbolic. However, this does not detract from the film in any way.

In this film, we can see that the director is very in love with inspiration (lnscsration), but at the same time is very serious about Methode. The same director's representative silent films also include "Mother" and "The Demise of Saint Petersburg", but unfortunately we cannot see them for a while. As for the performance of this film, it is also very good. Other aspects are omitted due to space constraints.

Review of "Sea Waves of Love" 314

— Yan Nan

LuxuryLlner

The plot of this film is very short, depicting a tragedy that occurs on a ship sailing across the Atlantic. A doctor's wife elopes on this ship, and the doctor tracks her down, securing a position as the "ship's duty doctor." He intends to win back his wife's affections. Before long, his wife and her lover turn against each other. She shoots her lover with a pistol, and then throws herself into the sea. By this time, the doctor has fallen in love with a nurse on the ship, so he does not feel the pain of losing his wife.

There are too many interspersed scenes in the film. The narrated events are two or three times more than the main plot, which relaxes the audience's focus and prevents concentration. At times, the impression is also exceptionally blurred. Furthermore, a major error was made due to the director's carelessness.

In reality, the script itself cannot be said to be unsound, and the meaning is good. It depicts "one wrong step leads to eternal regret" very thoroughly. The acting is also very good, with each actor fulfilling their duty. Good acting can be found in every foot of film. The distribution is very even, but because there are so many interspersed scenes, George Brent, Zita Johann, and Vivienne Osborne are comparatively the best.

Most of the supporting roles are in the interspersed scenes. These interspersed scenes represent the common phenomena in certain environments, and they are indeed very wonderful.

The director has some cleverness, and has fashionably learned many humorous elements.

Although there is not much dialogue, some of it is annoying. The scenery is good, and everywhere is consistent with the scenery one would expect on a ship. The lighting is extremely soft and aesthetically pleasing. Apart from the acting, the cinematography and editing are the best aspects. Many plain performances are made to feel not so plain. The close-ups and camera movements are also worth watching. The scenes of nature where the sky and water blend together are excellently framed. There are not many disjointed parts in the structure. Therefore, from a subjective artistic viewpoint, it should be considered an excellent choice, but in terms of storytelling, it is too convoluted.

The three short films shown with this film are all excellent. In the short films, one can also hear a long singing segment from Chevalier.

If you usually watch too many love films, then this film may give you a refreshing change of pace.

— Hui Jun

"No, Wayne," she faced him. "This is our last night. We must not see each other again."

Dazed and shocked, Wayne looked at her. Finally, he burst out a sentence:

"Emily! You… you don't love me? I've been thinking every day," he stammered, "thinking you would marry me! I was too confident..."

Emily smiled sadly. She shook her head slightly. Gently she said: "I'm so sorry, Wayne... If I had loved you like this when I first saw you... If I had known how sincere, tender, and earnest you were... I would never have let things get to this point... I love you, Wayne... but for nothing in the world, I won't marry you!"

Again he wanted to embrace her, but again she avoided him.

"Wayne, my love... I won't milk cows!" she said humorously, trying to force herself to calm down.

"There are farmhands to milk cows," he retorted.

"What kind of wife do you want," her voice was firm and persuasive, "There are many conditions I can't meet. I'm not worthy to be your wife. She, the girl in the countryside you told me about, is worthy... I know she will definitely be worthy of you."

"But I can't love her as much as I love you!" The young man was very disappointed.

"My love, my good man... Listen to someone with more experience than you, try to believe her... You are a different one among the men I know. I love you... but the first time I saw you, I knew I could never marry you, not even if I die... If we got married, who knows how much difficulty and pain would happen to us."

Wayne was silent. He was struggling to speak, but could not remember anything. This was the first time, crazily and drunkenly, he thought of Irene in the countryside. She wouldn't throw him away like this... He wished he could cry on Irene's shoulder.

He, palely and miserably, stared at Emily... as if she were a stranger. At this moment, he understood that he had lost her... understood that she would never belong to him... Still, everything about her washed over him like a tide.

"What we had before… doesn't that mean anything to you?" he asked deliriously, stretching out his arms to her in anguish. (To be continued)
